Third Objection: Eternal and Uniform Celestial Imagination
Third objection: eternal imagination, with al-Jurjani's refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third objection that celestial imagination could be eternal and uniform, and al-Jurjani's response that finite corporeal powers cannot sustain infinite motions.

Core Idea
Even if celestial imagination is eternal, finite powers cannot produce infinite motions.

The third objection proposes that the celestial sphere's imagination might be different from ours, remaining uniform and eternal, thus explaining the regularity of motions. Al-Jurjani counters that corporeal powers are finite in duration, number, and intensity, so they cannot be the basis for infinite motions. He also notes that if this argument were sound, it would undermine the proof for impressed souls.

Guided Path
1
Read the third objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the objector's suggestion that celestial imagination could be eternal and uniform.
The objector says 'Why may it not be that its imagination is different from our imagination?'
2
Understand the objector's challenge
The objector argues that if imagination can be perpetual and unchanging, then it can sustain eternal motions.
3
Analyze al-Jurjani's counter
He points out that corporeal powers are finite, so they cannot produce infinite motions. This refutes the objector's proposal.
He also uses a tu quoque: if this argument were correct, it would disprove impressed souls.
4
Note the final concession and deferred objection
The objector grants the point but raises a doubt about the immaterial locus of intellect, which is deferred to later discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والاعتراض) على هذا الدليل أن يقال : ( لا نسلم أنها ليست طبيعية وأنه يلزم ) من ذلك (كون المطلوب بالطبع مهروباً عنه بالطبع لجواز أن يكون المطلوب) في الحركة الطبيعة ( نفس الحركة ) لا حصول وضع معين فإن قيل : حقيقة الحركة هي التأدي إلي شيء آخر فلا تطلب لذاتها بل لغيرها قلنا الحركة عندنا عبارة عن كون الجوهر في آنين في مكانين فجاز كونها مطلوبة لذاتها ( سلمناه ) أي سلمنا أن الحركات الفلكية ليست طبيعية ( لكن لا نسلم أنها ليست قسرية قولكم القسر على خلاف الطبع) أي ما ليس فيه ميل طبيعي لا يقبل حركة قسرية ( ممنوع وقد مر ما في دليله من الخلل على أنه ليس يلزم من عدم كون حركاتها المستديرة طبيعية أن لا يكون لها ميل طبيعي مخالف لهذه الحركة ولا نسلم أيضاً أن القاسر هناك منحصر في الأفلاك حتى يلزم التشابه بل نقول : الحركة الحاصلة من بعضها في بعض تكون حركة عرضية لا قسرية ( سلمناه لكن لا نسلم أن التخيل لا ينتظم على حالة واحدة ولا يدوم سرمداً ( ولم لا يجوز أن يكون تخيله) أي تخيل الفلك (خلاف تخيلنا؟) فلا يختلف ولا ينقطع بل يستمر أزلاً وأبداً بتعاقب أفراد غير متناهية متعلقة بحركات متوافقة متماثلة. فإن قيل : القوى الجسمانية كما مر متناهية مدة وعدة وشدة فلا تستند إليها الحركات التي لا تتناهى . قلنا : قد مر أيضاً ما فيه ولو صح ذلك تعذر عليكم إثبات النفوس المنطبعة في الأجسام الفلكية ( سلمناه لكن لا نسلم أن محل العقل مجرد و ما سيأتي من برهانه ( سنتكلم عليه )
And an objection to this proof is to say: We do not grant that they are not natural, and that it follows from that that the naturally desired is naturally fled from, because it is possible that what is desired in natural motion is the motion itself, not attaining a particular position. If it is said: The reality of motion is passing to something else, so it is not desired for itself but for another, we say: Motion, in our view, is the existence of a substance in two moments in two places, so it is possible that it is desired for itself. We grant that—i.e., we grant that celestial motions are not natural. But we do not grant that they are not forced. Your statement that force is contrary to nature—i.e., that which has no natural inclination cannot receive forced motion—is denied, and what is in its proof of defect has already passed; moreover, the lack of natural circular motion does not imply they have no natural inclination contrary to this motion. And we also do not grant that the coercer there is restricted to the celestial spheres such that similarity would be necessary; rather, we say: The motion produced from some of them upon others is an accidental motion, not forced. We grant that, but we do not grant that imagination cannot remain in one state and continue eternally. Why may it not be that its imagination—i.e., the imagination of the sphere—is different from our imagination, so it does not differ or cease, but continues forever and ever through the succession of infinite individuals pertaining to similar, uniform motions? If it is said: Corporeal powers, as has passed, are finite in duration, number, and intensity, so motions that are infinite cannot be based upon them. We say: What is in that [proof] has also passed, and if that were correct, it would be impossible for you to prove the impressed souls in celestial bodies. We grant that, but we do not grant that the locus of intellect is immaterial, and what will come of its proof—we will discuss it there.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage records three objections to the proof that celestial motions are voluntary, with answers. First objection: Celestial motions might be natural if the object of natural desire is the motion itself rather than a position. Answer: Motion is defined as existence in two moments at two places, so it can be desired for itself. Second objection: Even if not natural, they could be forced; the lack of natural inclination does not preclude force, and the coercer need not be among the spheres. Answer: The premise about force and nature is denied, and accidental motion does not count as force. Third objection: Imagination (takhayyul) could be eternal and uniform if the celestial imagination differs from human imagination. The response: Corporeal powers are finite, so they cannot produce infinite motions. If this fails, the opponent would also fail to prove impressed souls. Finally, the interlocutor grants all but still doubts that the locus of intellect is immaterial, which will be addressed later.

Key Terms
تخيل (imagination)
قوى جسمانية (corporeal powers)
نفس منطبعة (impressed soul)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that a different kind of imagination could bypass the limitation of finite powers.
Correction: Al-Jurjani shows that regardless of imagination, the powers behind it are finite and cannot produce infinite effects.

Checkpoint
What reason does al-Jurjani give for why celestial imagination cannot produce infinite motions?
A) Imagination is inherently unstable.
B) Celestial spheres lack the capacity for imagination.
C) Corporeal powers are finite in duration, number, and intensity.
D) The motions are not voluntary.

Key Takeaway
Al-Jurjani refutes the third objection by pointing out that finite corporeal powers cannot sustain infinite motions, preserving the proof for celestial souls.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own daily efforts, do you truly believe they are sufficient without relying on Allah's infinite power? What would change if you internalized that all finite causes are ultimately dependent on Him?
?
What in your life do you assume will last forever—your health, relationships, or abilities—that is actually finite? How does this argument urge you to redirect your trust?
?
Al-Jurjani points out that if the objection were valid, it would undermine the proof for celestial souls. Is there a belief you hold that, if true, would invalidate a foundation of your faith? Are you willing to examine it honestly?

Opinions 1–4 on the Rational Soul: Substance, Subtle Bodies, and Powers
First four opinions on the rational soul enumerated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first four opinions on the nature of the rational soul and their key proponents.

Core Idea
The rational soul has been described as an indivisible substance, subtle bodies, a brain power, or three powers.

The author begins by listing the first four of nine well-known opinions on the nature of the rational soul. These range from a view that the soul is an indivisible substance in the heart to a tripartite division of powers located in different organs. Each opinion is presented concisely, setting the stage for the author's eventual critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the introductory lines
Read the first two sentences: 'المرصد الثالث – المقصد الثالث' up to 'المشهور منها تسعة'. This sets the context that nine opinions exist.
The phrase 'وقد اختلفوا فيها على تسعة أقوال' introduces the enumeration.
2
Examine the first opinion (Ibn al-Rawandi)
Read the description of the first opinion carefully. Notice the key terms: 'جوهر', 'فرد', 'قلب'. Understand the argument that the soul is indivisible and self-subsistent.
The proof involves denying immaterial substances.
3
Examine the second opinion (al-Nazzam)
Read about al-Nazzam's view: the soul consists of subtle bodies that pervade the body like rose water. Note the analogy and the claim of permanence.
The term 'أجزاء لطيفة' is important.
4
Compare opinions 3 and 4
Opinion 3 says the soul is a power in the brain (or heart). Opinion 4 divides it into three powers: animal, vegetative, and psychic. Identify the organs mentioned.
Note that opinion 4 adds a triadic structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الثالث - المقصد الثالث : في النفس الناطقة. وقد اختلفوا فيها على تسعة أقوال؟ [؟] المشهور منها تسعة: الأول: لابن الراوندي أنه يتجزأ في القلب لدليل عدم الانقسام مع نفي المجردات) يعني أنها جوهر لظهور قيامها بذاتها وغير منقسمة لما مر من تعقلها للبسائط وليست مجردة لامتناع وجود المجردات الممكنة فتكون جوهراً فرداً هو في القلب لأنه الذي ينسب إليه العلم. ( الثاني : للنظام أنه (أجزاء هي أجسام (لطيفة سارية في البدن ) سريان ماء الورد في الورد ( باقية من أول العمر إلى آخره لا يتطرق إليها تخلل وتبدل ) حتى إذا قطع عضو من البدن انقبض ما فيه من تلك الأجزاء إلى سائر الأعضاء ( إنما المتخلل والمتبدل ) من البدن (فضل ينضم إليه وينفصل عنه إذ كل أحد يعلم أنه باق ) من أول عمره إلى آخره ولا شك أن المتبدل ليس كذلك. ( الثالث : أنه قوة في الدماغ وقيل : في القلب . الرابع : أنه ثلاث قوى إحداها في القلب وهي الحيوانية، والثانية في الكبد وهي النباتية والثالثة في الدماغ وهي النفسانية الخامس : أنه الهيكل المخصوص ) وهو المختار عند جمهور المتكلمين ( السادس : أنه الأخلاط الأربعة المعتدلة كماً وكيفاً، السابع : أنه اعتدال المزاج النوعي . الثامن: أنه الدم المعتدل إذ بكثرته واعتداله تقوى الحياة وبالعكس التاسع : أنه الهواء إذ بانقطاعه طرفة عين تنقطع الحياة فالبدن بمنزلة الزق المنفوخ فيه ) واعلم أن شيئاً من ذلك) الذي رويناه ( لم يقم عليه دليل وما ذكروه لا يصلح للتعويل عليه .
The third observation – the third purpose: on the rational soul. And they disagreed about it in nine opinions? [؟] The well-known among them are nine: The first: by Ibn al-Rawandi: that it is divisible in the heart due to the proof of indivisibility with the denial of immaterial substances; meaning that it is a substance because of its apparent self-subsistence and its indivisibility, due to what has passed of its intellection of simple things, and it is not immaterial because of the impossibility of the existence of possible immaterial substances; so it is an individual substance in the heart because it is that to which knowledge is attributed. The second: by al-Nazzam: that it is parts which are subtle bodies pervading the body like the pervasion of rose water in the rose, remaining from the beginning of life to its end, interpenetration and change do not affect them; so if a limb is cut from the body, what is in it of those parts contracts to the other limbs; only the excess that joins and separates from the body is what interpenetrates and changes, for everyone knows that he remains from the beginning of his life to its end, and there is no doubt that the changing is not so. The third: that it is a power in the brain, and it is said: in the heart. The fourth: that it is three powers: one in the heart which is the animal, the second in the liver which is the vegetative, and the third in the brain which is the psychic. The fifth: that it is the specific structure, and it is the chosen view of the majority of theologians. The sixth: that it is the four humors balanced in quantity and quality. The seventh: that it is the balance of the specific temperament. The eighth: that it is the balanced blood, for by its abundance and balance life is strengthened, and conversely. The ninth: that it is air, for by its cessation for a blink life ceases, so the body is like an inflated waterskin. And know that none of that which we have narrated has proof established for it, and what they mentioned is not suitable for reliance.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration and critique of nine opinions on the nature of the rational soul (النفس الناطقة). The author lists the views of various theologians and philosophers, each very briefly. The first opinion, from Ibn al-Rawandi, holds that the soul is an indivisible substance located in the heart. The second, from al-Nazzam, says it is composed of subtle bodies that permeate the body and remain unchanged. The third says it is a power in the brain or heart. The fourth divides it into three powers: animal (in the heart), vegetative (in the liver), and psychic (in the brain). The fifth identifies it with the specific structure (الهيكل المخصوص), which is the preferred view of the majority of theologians (جمهور المتكلمين). The sixth says it is the balanced four humors. The seventh says it is the balance of the species temperament. The eighth says it is balanced blood. The ninth says it is air. After listing these, the author dismisses all of them: none have proof, and what they say is not reliable. This sets the stage for the author's own position, which will follow.

جوهر
أجزاء لطيفة
قوة في الدماغ
قلب
ثلاث قوى
حيوانية
نباتية
نفسانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first opinion (Ibn al-Rawandi), where is the rational soul located?
A) In the brain
B) In the heart
C) In the liver
D) In the entire body

Key Takeaway
The first four opinions view the soul as either an indivisible substance, subtle bodies, a single power, or a triad of powers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that some scholars locate the soul in the heart, others in the brain, and others as a subtle body pervading you. Where do you personally feel your 'self' resides – in your thoughts, your emotions, or your physical sensations? When you act, which part of you are you actually obeying?
?
Al-Nazzam said the soul's parts remain unchanged from birth to death. What part of you has never changed? Is that your soul, or is it something else? If your beliefs, memories, and body have all changed, then what is the constant 'you' that you call 'I'?
?
The fourth opinion says you have three distinct powers: animal (drives), vegetative (growth), and psychic (awareness). Which of these three is currently dominating your life? Are you feeding your animal desires, your vegetative habits, or your conscious soul? Be specific: what did you do today that served only your highest self?

Opinions 5–9 and Dismissal: From Structure to Air
Last five opinions and dismissal of all nine views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the last five opinions on the rational soul and why the author dismisses all nine as unsupported.

Core Idea
The soul has been identified with the body's structure, humors, temperament, blood, or air—but none withstand scrutiny.

The author concludes his enumeration with opinions that locate the soul in bodily structures, balanced humors, temperament, blood, or air. After listing them, he delivers a decisive verdict: none of these views have any proof and are not worthy of reliance. This sets the stage for his own position on the nature of the rational soul.

Guided Path
1
Read opinions 5–9
Read from 'الخامس: أنه الهيكل المخصوص' to 'التاسع: أنه الهواء'. Note the diversity: from physical structure to air.
Opinion 5 is noted as the preferred view of the majority of theologians.
2
Understand the dismissal
Read the final sentence: 'واعلم أن شيئاً من ذلك لم يقم عليه دليل'. This is the author's rejection of all nine opinions.
The phrase 'لا يصلح للتعويل عليه' is strong criticism.
3
Reflect on the pattern
Notice that the opinions move from immaterial to material explanations. The author rejects them all, implying a different approach.
Think about why none of these are considered proof.

?

The rejection of the 'specific structure' opinion challenges you to pinpoint your own essence. Commit to one action today that affirms your soul is more than your physical form.

The Two Sub-Possibilities for Multiple Souls Before Attachment
Analyzes the 'multiple souls' branch in the proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why souls cannot be multiple before attachment by themselves or by a previous body, and how this leads to rejecting metempsychosis.

Core Idea
If souls were multiple before bodies, they would either be distinct by essence (making each a unique species) or by a previous body (leading to metempsychosis).

The author begins a proof by elimination to determine the state of the rational soul before its attachment to the body. The first major branch considers whether souls are multiple prior to attachment. Within this branch, two sub-possibilities are examined: either their distinction is by their own essences or by an external factor. This lesson explores these sub-possibilities and shows why both are untenable, thereby eliminating the possibility of pre-existing multiple souls.

Guided Path
1
Understand the proof structure
Recognize that the author is using a logical division (taqsīm) to exhaust possibilities. The first division is between souls being multiple or one before attachment. This lesson covers the 'multiple' branch.
The entire proof hinges on showing that each possibility leads to an absurdity, leaving only one conclusion.
2
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note that the passage first assumes souls are multiple, then asks how they are distinct.
Pay attention to the parentheses in the Arabic; they indicate the author's own clarifications.
3
Analyze the first sub-case: distinction by essence
If souls are distinct by themselves, each soul becomes a unique species (nawʿ munḥaṣir) confined to one individual. This would imply all souls differ essentially, which contradicts the observed similarity among human souls.
The author says that even if not all are similar, there must be at least two similar souls among all.
4
Analyze the second sub-case: distinction by body
If distinction is not by essence, it must be by the receiver and its accidents, i.e., the body. But then the soul would have been attached to another body before this one, leading to metempsychosis (tanāsukh), which the author promises to refute later.
Metempsychosis is the transmigration of souls from one body to another.
5
Summarize the refutation
Both sub-cases are shown to be false. Therefore, the possibility that souls are multiple before attachment is rejected.
This sets the stage for considering the alternative: souls being one before attachment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تكون قبل التعلق بالبدن متعددة (متمايزة أولا فإن كانت متمايزة فتمايزها) وتعينها (إما بذواتها أولا بذواتها فإن كان (بذواتها أو بلوازمها) فتكون كل نفس) من النفوس البشرية (نوعاً منحصراً في الشخص الواحد) فيلزم اختلاف كل نفسين بالحقيقة. وإنه باطل إذ لو لم نقل بأن كلها متماثلة فلا أقل من أن يوجد (فيما بين الجميع) نفسان متماثلان. وإن كان تمايزها (لا بذواتها) كان بالقابل وما يكتنفه كما تقدم من أن تعدد أفراد النوع الواحد معلل بقابله والأعراض المكتنفة به (ومادتها البدن) فتكون متعلقة قبل هذا البدن (ببدن آخر) ويلزم التناسخ أي انتقالها من بدن إلى آخر وسنبطله. وإن لم تكن قبل التعلق (متمايزة) بل كانت واحدة فبعد التعلق إن بقيت (على وحدتها) كما كانت كانت نفس زيد هي بعينها نفس عمرو فيلزم أن يشتركا في صفات النفس من العلم والقدرة واللذة والألم وسائر الصفات وأنه باطل بالضرورة. وإن لم تبق كما كانت بل تكثرت لزم التجزؤ والانقسام ولا يتصور إلا فيما له مقدار وحجم فلا تكون مجردة بل مادية. وأيضاً فقد عدمت بذلك التجزؤ والانقسام (تلك الهوية) (الواحدة القديمة) وحصلت هويتان أخريان حادثتان ويلزم المطلوب وهو أن النفوس المتعلقة بالأبدان حادثة.
They [the souls] are before attachment to the body multiple, distinct first. If they are distinct, their distinction and determination is either by themselves or by their accidents. If by themselves, every soul from human souls would be a species confined to a single individual, which necessitates that every two souls differ in essence. And this is false, for if we do not say that all of them are similar, then at least there exist among all of them two similar souls. And if their distinction is not by themselves, then it is by the receiver and what surrounds it as previously mentioned: that the multiplicity of individuals of a single species is explained by its receiver and the surrounding accidents, and their matter is the body. Then they would be attached before this body to another body, and metempsychosis follows, meaning their transfer from one body to another, and we will refute it. And if they were not distinct before attachment but were one, then after attachment, if they remain in their unity as they were, then Zayd's soul would be the very same as Amr's soul, which would necessitate that they share in the attributes of the soul: knowledge, power, pleasure, pain, and all attributes, and that is impossible by necessity. And if they do not remain as they were but become multiple, then division and partition would be necessary, and this can only be conceived for something having magnitude and size, so they would not be non-material but material. Also, that single eternal identity would cease to exist by that division and partition, and two other originated identities would arise, and the required conclusion follows: that souls attached to bodies are originated.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a proof by elimination (taqsīm) of the possible states of the rational soul before its attachment to the body. The author considers two main possibilities: either souls are multiple before attachment or they are one. If multiple, their distinction (tamāyuz) must be explained either by their own essences or by something external like the body. If by themselves, each soul becomes a unique species (nawʿ munḥaṣir fī al-shakhṣ al-wāḥid), so all souls would differ in essence—but we know souls are similar in type. If by the body, then the soul must have been attached to a previous body, leading to metempsychosis (tanāsukh), which will be rejected later. If souls were one before attachment, then after attachment either they remain one—so Zayd and Amr would share the same soul, which is absurd—or they become multiple, requiring division (tajazzuʾ) which is impossible for a non-material substance. Therefore, the original identity is destroyed and two new identities arise, proving that souls are originated (ḥāditha).

Key Terms
تمايز (tamāyuz)
نوع منحصر (nawʿ munḥaṣir)
تناسخ (tanāsukh)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Souls are pre-eternal and exist as multiple distinct entities before being attached to bodies.
Correction: The passage logically refutes this by showing that if they were multiple, they would have to be distinct either by essence (making each unique species, which contradicts observed similarity) or by body (leading to metempsychosis, which is false).

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if souls are distinct by themselves before attachment?
A) Each soul becomes a unique species.
B) They would be material.
C) They would be identical.
D) They would be infinite.

Key Takeaway
Souls cannot be multiple before attachment because both ways of explaining their multiplicity lead to false conclusions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every human soul shares the same essence, what does that mean for how you view your own worth compared to others? How can you practice seeing every person as fundamentally equal in soul?
?
The passage proves that souls cannot be pre-existing individuals. How does this truth affect your understanding of your identity? Are you defined more by your body and circumstances than you thought? How can you live with gratitude for the specific body and life God has given you?
?
The argument eliminates the possibility of your soul existing before this life. Does that change how you think about your purpose here? How can you focus more on your current, finite opportunity to know and worship Allah, rather than dwelling on speculative pre-existence?

The Impossibility of Souls Being One Before Attachment
Analyzes the 'one soul' branch and concludes souls are created.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the soul cannot have been a single entity before attachment, and how this leads to the conclusion that souls are created (ḥāditha).

Core Idea
If souls were one before bodies, they would either remain one (making individuals identical) or become multiple (requiring division impossible for non-material entities).

Having rejected the possibility of multiple souls before attachment, the author now turns to the alternative: that all souls were a single entity prior to attachment. This lesson examines what follows when that single soul attaches to multiple bodies. Two scenarios are considered: either the soul remains one, or it becomes multiple. Both lead to impossibilities, ultimately proving that souls are originated entities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for this lesson
Read the Arabic and translation for the second part of the proof. This continues from the previous lesson, now assuming souls were one before attachment.
The passage begins 'If they were not distinct before attachment but were one'.
2
Understand the first sub-case: remaining one
If the single soul remains one after attachment to many bodies, then the souls of Zayd and Amr would be identical. This would mean they share all attributes (knowledge, power, pain, etc.), which is impossible by necessity.
This is a contradiction because we observe that individuals have distinct experiences and knowledge.
3
Understand the second sub-case: becoming multiple
If the single soul becomes multiple, it must undergo division (tajazzuʾ). Only physical objects can be divided; a non-material (mujarrad) substance cannot. Therefore, the soul would have to be material, which contradicts its spiritual nature.
Additionally, the original identity perishes and two new identities arise, proving that the souls are originated (ḥāditha), not eternal.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Both sub-cases are impossible. Therefore, the assumption that souls are one before attachment is false. The only remaining conclusion is that souls are originated and come into existence with the body.
This is the central point of the entire argument: the soul is created, not pre-eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تكون قبل التعلق بالبدن متعددة (متمايزة أولا فإن كانت متمايزة فتمايزها) وتعينها (إما بذواتها أولا بذواتها فإن كان (بذواتها أو بلوازمها) فتكون كل نفس) من النفوس البشرية (نوعاً منحصراً في الشخص الواحد) فيلزم اختلاف كل نفسين بالحقيقة. وإنه باطل إذ لو لم نقل بأن كلها متماثلة فلا أقل من أن يوجد (فيما بين الجميع) نفسان متماثلان. وإن كان تمايزها (لا بذواتها) كان بالقابل وما يكتنفه كما تقدم من أن تعدد أفراد النوع الواحد معلل بقابله والأعراض المكتنفة به (ومادتها البدن) فتكون متعلقة قبل هذا البدن (ببدن آخر) ويلزم التناسخ أي انتقالها من بدن إلى آخر وسنبطله. وإن لم تكن قبل التعلق (متمايزة) بل كانت واحدة فبعد التعلق إن بقيت (على وحدتها) كما كانت كانت نفس زيد هي بعينها نفس عمرو فيلزم أن يشتركا في صفات النفس من العلم والقدرة واللذة والألم وسائر الصفات وأنه باطل بالضرورة. وإن لم تبق كما كانت بل تكثرت لزم التجزؤ والانقسام ولا يتصور إلا فيما له مقدار وحجم فلا تكون مجردة بل مادية. وأيضاً فقد عدمت بذلك التجزؤ والانقسام (تلك الهوية) (الواحدة القديمة) وحصلت هويتان أخريان حادثتان ويلزم المطلوب وهو أن النفوس المتعلقة بالأبدان حادثة.
They [the souls] are before attachment to the body multiple, distinct first. If they are distinct, their distinction and determination is either by themselves or by their accidents. If by themselves, every soul from human souls would be a species confined to a single individual, which necessitates that every two souls differ in essence. And this is false, for if we do not say that all of them are similar, then at least there exist among all of them two similar souls. And if their distinction is not by themselves, then it is by the receiver and what surrounds it as previously mentioned: that the multiplicity of individuals of a single species is explained by its receiver and the surrounding accidents, and their matter is the body. Then they would be attached before this body to another body, and metempsychosis follows, meaning their transfer from one body to another, and we will refute it. And if they were not distinct before attachment but were one, then after attachment, if they remain in their unity as they were, then Zayd's soul would be the very same as Amr's soul, which would necessitate that they share in the attributes of the soul: knowledge, power, pleasure, pain, and all attributes, and that is impossible by necessity. And if they do not remain as they were but become multiple, then division and partition would be necessary, and this can only be conceived for something having magnitude and size, so they would not be non-material but material. Also, that single eternal identity would cease to exist by that division and partition, and two other originated identities would arise, and the required conclusion follows: that souls attached to bodies are originated.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a proof by elimination (taqsīm) of the possible states of the rational soul before its attachment to the body. The author considers two main possibilities: either souls are multiple before attachment or they are one. If multiple, their distinction (tamāyuz) must be explained either by their own essences or by something external like the body. If by themselves, each soul becomes a unique species (nawʿ munḥaṣir fī al-shakhṣ al-wāḥid), so all souls would differ in essence—but we know souls are similar in type. If by the body, then the soul must have been attached to a previous body, leading to metempsychosis (tanāsukh), which will be rejected later. If souls were one before attachment, then after attachment either they remain one—so Zayd and Amr would share the same soul, which is absurd—or they become multiple, requiring division (tajazzuʾ) which is impossible for a non-material substance. Therefore, the original identity is destroyed and two new identities arise, proving that souls are originated (ḥāditha).

تجزؤ (tajazzuʾ)
هوية واحدة قديمة (identity single eternal)
حادثة (ḥāditha)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul could be a single pre-eternal substance that divides into many souls upon attachment to bodies.
Correction: Division is impossible for non-material entities; also, the original identity would perish, indicating creation, not pre-eternality.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if the single soul remains one after attachment?
A) Zayd and Amr would have identical souls.
B) The soul becomes material.
C) The soul would be divided.
D) The soul would cease to exist.

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of souls being one before attachment, combined with the previous rejection of multiplicity, proves that souls are created entities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your soul was created by Allah at a specific moment in time (when your body was formed), what does that mean about the unique purpose He has for you? How does this knowledge change the way you live each day, knowing your soul has no previous existence or karma to carry?
?
The argument shows that your soul is not part of a larger universal soul but is individually created. How does being a unique and distinct soul before Allah affect your understanding of personal accountability? What would you say to your Creator if He asked you: 'I created this soul for you—what have you done with it?'
?
Imagine that before your conception, your soul did not exist at all. Now you exist as a conscious being with knowledge, power, pleasure, and pain. Who gave you these attributes? How can you use them today in a way that acknowledges your soul's createdness and returns gratitude to its Creator?

First Proof: The Matter Argument and Its Refutation
First of three proofs for the soul's pre-eternity and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first argument for the soul's pre-eternity based on matter and how it is refuted by distinguishing between types of matter.

Core Idea
Origination implies matter, but matter doesn't make the soul material.

The first proof claims that if the soul were originated, it would require matter, making it material. However, the refutation shows that the matter required by origination is broader and can include attachment to matter without the soul itself being material. This lesson examines this argument and its key distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation of the first proof and refutation.
Notice how the opponent's argument is presented concisely.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponent argues that every originated thing has matter, so if the soul were originated, it would be material. Since the soul is immaterial, it must be pre-eternal.
3
Understand the refutation
The refutation concedes the implication but expands 'matter' to include matter of subsistence and matter of attachment. The soul is attached to matter, not subsisting in it, so it can be immaterial yet originated.
This distinction is crucial for later arguments in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
احتج الخصم على قدمها بوجوه ثلاثة: الأول: إن كل حادث له مادة فلو كانت النفس حادثة كانت مادية لا مجردة. قلنا: بعد تسليم الملازمة تلك المادة التي يستلزمها الحدوث أعم (مادة يحل الحادث فيها أو يتعلق بها) والمتعلق بالمادة يجوز أن يكون مجردا بحسب ذاته. الثاني: لو لم تكن الناطقة أزلية لم تكن أبدية أيضاً والتالي باطل اتفاقاً. وأما الملازمة فلأنها إذا كانت حادثة يزول وجودها لأن كل كائن فاسد. والجواب: المنع ومعنى القضية المذكورة أن كل حادث فهو في حد ذاته قابل للعدم وليس يلزم منه طريانه عليه لجواز أن يمتنع عدمه لغيره أبدا. الثالث: يلزم عدم تناهي الأبدان والصواب عدم تناهي النفوس وذلك لأنها إذا كانت حادثة كان حدوثها بحدوث الأبدان التي هي شرط فيضانها من المبدأ القديم، والأبدان غير متناهية لا استنادها إلى اقتضاء الأدوار الفلكية التي لا تتناهى فتكون النفوس البشرية غير متناهية أيضاً لكن لا استحالة في لاتناهي الأبدان والأدوار لأنها متعاقبة بخلاف النفوس فإنها باقية بعد المفارقة فيلزم اجتماع أمور موجودة غير متناهية وهو محال بالتطبيق. والجواب شرط امتناعه الترتب الطبيعي أو الوضعي كما مر. والنفوس الناطقة وإن كانت موجودة مجتمعة إلا أنها غير مترتبة فيجوز لا تناهيها.
The opponent argued for its pre-eternity with three aspects: First: Every originated thing has a matter. If the soul were originated, it would be material, not non-material. We said: After conceding the implication, that matter which origination necessitates is broader: matter in which the originated thing subsists or to which it is attached, and that which is attached to matter may be non-material according to its essence. Second: If the rational soul were not pre-eternal, it would not be everlasting either, and the consequent is false by agreement. As for the implication, it is because if it were originated, its existence would perish, since everything that comes to be is corruptible. The answer: denial. The meaning of the mentioned proposition is that every originated thing is in itself receptive to non-existence, but it does not necessarily follow that non-existence occurs to it, because it is possible that its non-existence is prevented by another eternally. Third: The non-finiteness of bodies would be necessary, but the correct view is the non-finiteness of souls. That is because if they are originated, their origination occurs with the origination of bodies which are the condition for their emanation from the pre-eternal principle. Bodies are infinite due to their dependence on the requirement of celestial cycles which are infinite. Thus human souls would also be infinite. However, there is no impossibility in the infinity of bodies and cycles because they are sequential, unlike souls, which remain after separation. Hence the coexistence of an infinite number of existing things would follow, which is impossible by the method of correlation (taṭbīq). The answer: The condition for its impossibility is natural or positional ordering, as previously mentioned. Rational souls, although they exist collectively, are not ordered, so their infinity is permissible.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage presents three objections (wujūh) from an opponent who argues that the soul is pre-eternal (qadīma), along with their refutations. The first objection: every originated thing requires matter, so if the soul were originated, it would be material. The answer: the matter required by origination is broader—it can be matter in which the thing subsists or to which it is attached; a non-material substance can be attached to matter. The second objection: if the soul is not pre-eternal, it cannot be everlasting; but the soul is everlasting by consensus. The implication is that whatever is originated perishes. The answer: denial of the implication—an originated thing is inherently possible of non-existence, but it may be prevented from perishing by another (e.g., God's power). The third objection: if souls are originated, they are originated with bodies, which are infinite due to celestial cycles; thus souls would be infinite. But bodies are sequential, so their infinity is not problematic, whereas souls coexist without order, making an infinite actual collection impossible. The answer: the impossibility of infinite coexistence only applies when things are naturally or positionally ordered; souls are not ordered, so infinite souls are possible.

Key Terms
قدم (pre-eternity)
مادة (matter)
حادث (originated)
مجرد (non-material)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That if something is attached to matter, it must itself be material.
Correction: Attachment to matter does not entail materiality; the soul is attached to the body but is immaterial.

Checkpoint
According to the refutation of the first proof, what does the 'matter' required for origination include?
A) Only matter in which the thing subsists.
B) Only matter to which the thing is attached.
C) Both matter in which the thing subsists and matter to which it is attached.
D) Neither.

Key Takeaway
The soul can be originated and immaterial because origination only requires attachment to matter, not material composition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just seen a proof that the soul could be created and immaterial. Does the createdness of your soul feel real to you, or do you live as if your soul is self-sufficient? What one habit could you change today to remember that your soul is contingent upon Allah?
?
The opponent assumed that being immaterial meant being eternal. Are there aspects of your faith that you treat as permanent simply because they feel 'spiritual'? For example, do your good deeds feel like they have lasting value even if your intention wavers? How can you renew your reliance on Allah's mercy rather than the apparent 'eternality' of spiritual feelings?
?
The refutation teaches that attachment to matter does not make one material. Your soul is attached to your body, yet your true identity is beyond it. When you sin with your body, do you feel that your soul is tainted, or do you separate the action from your essence? What step will you take today to remind yourself that your soul is pure and capable of repentance, despite bodily transgressions?

Second Proof: The Implication of Everlastingness and Its Refutation
Second proof for the soul's pre-eternity and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second argument that if the soul is not pre-eternal it cannot be everlasting, and the refutation that origination does not guarantee eventual annihilation.

Core Idea
An originated thing is not necessarily subject to annihilation.

The second proof argues that if the soul were originated, it would eventually perish, but the soul is agreed to be everlasting. The refutation denies this implication by explaining that origination only makes non-existence possible, not necessary. This lesson clarifies that something originated can be sustained forever by an external cause.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation of the second proof and its refutation.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponent argues: If the soul is not pre-eternal, then it cannot be everlasting; because all originated things are corruptible. Since the soul is everlasting by consensus, it must be pre-eternal.
3
Understand the refutation
The refutation denies the implication (al-manʿ). It explains that 'every originated thing is corruptible' means only that it has the potential to cease, not that it actually will. An external cause (e.g., God) can sustain it forever.
This is a key distinction between possibility and actuality in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
احتج الخصم على قدمها بوجوه ثلاثة: الأول: إن كل حادث له مادة فلو كانت النفس حادثة كانت مادية لا مجردة. قلنا: بعد تسليم الملازمة تلك المادة التي يستلزمها الحدوث أعم (مادة يحل الحادث فيها أو يتعلق بها) والمتعلق بالمادة يجوز أن يكون مجردا بحسب ذاته. الثاني: لو لم تكن الناطقة أزلية لم تكن أبدية أيضاً والتالي باطل اتفاقاً. وأما الملازمة فلأنها إذا كانت حادثة يزول وجودها لأن كل كائن فاسد. والجواب: المنع ومعنى القضية المذكورة أن كل حادث فهو في حد ذاته قابل للعدم وليس يلزم منه طريانه عليه لجواز أن يمتنع عدمه لغيره أبدا. الثالث: يلزم عدم تناهي الأبدان والصواب عدم تناهي النفوس وذلك لأنها إذا كانت حادثة كان حدوثها بحدوث الأبدان التي هي شرط فيضانها من المبدأ القديم، والأبدان غير متناهية لا استنادها إلى اقتضاء الأدوار الفلكية التي لا تتناهى فتكون النفوس البشرية غير متناهية أيضاً لكن لا استحالة في لاتناهي الأبدان والأدوار لأنها متعاقبة بخلاف النفوس فإنها باقية بعد المفارقة فيلزم اجتماع أمور موجودة غير متناهية وهو محال بالتطبيق. والجواب شرط امتناعه الترتب الطبيعي أو الوضعي كما مر. والنفوس الناطقة وإن كانت موجودة مجتمعة إلا أنها غير مترتبة فيجوز لا تناهيها.
The opponent argued for its pre-eternity with three aspects: First: Every originated thing has a matter. If the soul were originated, it would be material, not non-material. We said: After conceding the implication, that matter which origination necessitates is broader: matter in which the originated thing subsists or to which it is attached, and that which is attached to matter may be non-material according to its essence. Second: If the rational soul were not pre-eternal, it would not be everlasting either, and the consequent is false by agreement. As for the implication, it is because if it were originated, its existence would perish, since everything that comes to be is corruptible. The answer: denial. The meaning of the mentioned proposition is that every originated thing is in itself receptive to non-existence, but it does not necessarily follow that non-existence occurs to it, because it is possible that its non-existence is prevented by another eternally. Third: The non-finiteness of bodies would be necessary, but the correct view is the non-finiteness of souls. That is because if they are originated, their origination occurs with the origination of bodies which are the condition for their emanation from the pre-eternal principle. Bodies are infinite due to their dependence on the requirement of celestial cycles which are infinite. Thus human souls would also be infinite. However, there is no impossibility in the infinity of bodies and cycles because they are sequential, unlike souls, which remain after separation. Hence the coexistence of an infinite number of existing things would follow, which is impossible by the method of correlation (taṭbīq). The answer: The condition for its impossibility is natural or positional ordering, as previously mentioned. Rational souls, although they exist collectively, are not ordered, so their infinity is permissible.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage presents three objections (wujūh) from an opponent who argues that the soul is pre-eternal (qadīma), along with their refutations. The first objection: every originated thing requires matter, so if the soul were originated, it would be material. The answer: the matter required by origination is broader—it can be matter in which the thing subsists or to which it is attached; a non-material substance can be attached to matter. The second objection: if the soul is not pre-eternal, it cannot be everlasting; but the soul is everlasting by consensus. The implication is that whatever is originated perishes. The answer: denial of the implication—an originated thing is inherently possible of non-existence, but it may be prevented from perishing by another (e.g., God's power). The third objection: if souls are originated, they are originated with bodies, which are infinite due to celestial cycles; thus souls would be infinite. But bodies are sequential, so their infinity is not problematic, whereas souls coexist without order, making an infinite actual collection impossible. The answer: the impossibility of infinite coexistence only applies when things are naturally or positionally ordered; souls are not ordered, so infinite souls are possible.

Key Terms
أزلية (pre-eternal)
أبدية (everlasting)
حادث (originated)
فاسد (corruptible)
قابل للعدم (receptive to non-existence)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That every originated thing must inevitably perish.
Correction: An originated thing is only potentially perishable; it may be sustained forever by an external cause.

Checkpoint
What is the key point in the refutation of the second proof?
A) The soul is not originated.
B) An originated thing is not necessarily subject to annihilation.
C) The soul is not everlasting.
D) The opponent's premise is false.

Key Takeaway
An originated thing can be everlasting if its nonexistence is eternally prevented by another.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The opponent argued that if the soul is not eternal from the past, it cannot continue forever. In your daily life, do you sometimes act as if your own goodness or achievements are self-sustaining, forgetting that God's will is what keeps them alive? What is one area where you need to consciously rely on God's sustaining power right now?
?
The refutation shows that God can prevent an originated thing from perishing. Is there a persistent sin or weakness in your life that you have assumed is inevitable, like a 'corruptible' part of you that cannot be changed? How does this lesson challenge that assumption, and what step will you take today to trust that God can eternally prevent its destruction?
